## *Star Wars: The Clone Wars*

## Production information

### Format

[Animated](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Animation "wikipedia:Animation")[[1]](#cite_note-Ambush-1)

### Episode count

133

### No. of seasons

7

### Run time

Approx. 23 minutes per episode[[2]](#cite_note-CIVblog-2) (30-min time slot)

### Network(s)

* [Cartoon Network](/wiki/Cartoon_Network "Cartoon Network")[[3]](#cite_note-ann-3)
* [TNT](/wiki/Turner_Network_Television "Turner Network Television")[[3]](#cite_note-ann-3)
* [Netflix](/wiki/Netflix "Netflix")[[4]](#cite_note-TCW_on_Netflix-4)
* [Disney+](/wiki/Disney%2B "Disney+")[[5]](#cite_note-TCW_Revival-5)

## Chronological information

### Timeline

[22 BBY](/wiki/22_BBY "22 BBY")–[19 BBY](/wiki/19_BBY "19 BBY")[[49]](#cite_note-Timelines-49)

[[Source]](https://starwars.fandom.com/wiki/Template:TelevisionSeries)
***Star Wars: The Clone Wars*** is an [animated television series](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Animated_series "wikipedia:Animated series") set between the events of [Star Wars: Episode II Attack of the Clones](/wiki/Star_Wars:_Episode_II_Attack_of_the_Clones "Star Wars: Episode II Attack of the Clones") and [Star Wars: Episode III Revenge of the Sith](/wiki/Star_Wars:_Episode_III_Revenge_of_the_Sith "Star Wars: Episode III Revenge of the Sith"). The series aired on [Cartoon Network](/wiki/Cartoon_Network "Cartoon Network") for five seasons from [2008](/wiki/2008 "2008") to [2013](/wiki/2013 "2013"), while an abridged sixth season was released through [Netflix](/wiki/Netflix "Netflix") in [2014](/wiki/2014 "2014"). The final, [seventh season](/wiki/The_Clone_Wars:_Season_Seven "The Clone Wars: Season Seven") was released on [Disney+](/wiki/Disney%2B "Disney+") in [2020](/wiki/2020 "2020").

## Development[]

 [![(left to right) George Lucas, Dave Filoni, and Catherine Winder discuss the series.](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/9/93/LWF.jpg/revision/latest?cb=20070804022222) [![(left to right) George Lucas, Dave Filoni, and Catherine Winder discuss the series.](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/9/93/LWF.jpg/revision/latest/scale-to-width-down/250?cb=20070804022222)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/9/93/LWF.jpg/revision/latest?cb=20070804022222) 

(left to right) George Lucas, Dave Filoni, and Catherine Winder discuss the series.

 

[George Lucas](/wiki/George_Lucas "George Lucas") first had the idea for a [Clone Wars](/wiki/Clone_Wars "Clone Wars") animated series in [2002](/wiki/2002 "2002").[[50]](#cite_note-nyt-50) *[Star Wars: Clone Wars](/wiki/Star_Wars:_Clone_Wars "Star Wars: Clone Wars")* aired on [Cartoon Network](/wiki/Cartoon_Network "Cartoon Network")[[51]](#cite_note-cwannouncement-51) from [2003](/wiki/2003 "2003") to [2005](/wiki/2005 "2005"),[[52]](#cite_note-Chapter_Archive-52) produced by [Genndy Tartakovsky](/wiki/Genndy_Tartakovsky "Genndy Tartakovsky").[[53]](#cite_note-Cast-53) Lucas then announced *Star Wars: The Clone Wars* at April 2005's [Celebration III](/wiki/Celebration_III "Celebration III"), where he described *Clone Wars* as a "pilot television series" and said that *The Clone Wars* would "take that and turn it into a 3-D animated version full series."[[54]](#cite_note-celebration-54) [Dave Filoni](/wiki/Dave_Filoni "Dave Filoni") was hired as supervising director, and was familiar with previous *Star Wars* animation projects.[[55]](#cite_note-CBR-55)[[56]](#cite_note-scifi-56) Filoni's initial idea for the series revolved around a recurring cast of characters who traveled aboard a spaceship similar to the *[Millennium Falcon](/wiki/Millennium_Falcon "Millennium Falcon")*; the ship's crew would have included a smuggler, his girlfriend, a [Gungan](/wiki/Gungan "Gungan") named Lunker, a [Jedi](/wiki/Jedi "Jedi") [padawan](/wiki/Padawan "Padawan") named Ashla, and her [Jedi Master](/wiki/Jedi_Master "Jedi Master"). This early concept for *The Clone Wars* was designed not to interfere with existing continuity, and as such would have included only occasional appearances from film characters, such as [Obi-Wan Kenobi](/wiki/Obi-Wan_Kenobi "Obi-Wan Kenobi") and [Anakin Skywalker](/wiki/Anakin_Skywalker "Anakin Skywalker"). However, once Lucas became involved, he decided that the show would focus on the film characters, but would also include some of Filoni's ideas, such as Ashla (whose name was ultimately changed to [Ahsoka](/wiki/Ahsoka_Tano "Ahsoka Tano")).[[57]](#cite_note-TCW_Art-57)

By [February](/wiki/February "February") [2006](/wiki/2006 "2006"), [Lucasfilm Animation](/wiki/Lucasfilm_Animation "Lucasfilm Animation") was working on animation tests and initial scripts, with Lucas playing a large part in the entire process.[[58]](#cite_note-steve-58)[[2]](#cite_note-CIVblog-2) The crew used [Autodesk](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Autodesk "wikipedia:Autodesk") [software](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Software "wikipedia:Software") to animate both the film and the series. The [Maya](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Maya_(software) "wikipedia:Maya (software)") [3D modeling](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/3D_modeler "wikipedia:3D modeler") program was used to create highly detailed worlds, characters, and creatures.[[59]](#cite_note-Autodesk-59) Lucas and the animation team used this to create Zviz, a system that allowed the animation team complete freedom in framing shots.[[60]](#cite_note-awn-60)[[61]](#cite_note-EW-61) Script, character design, and art direction were completed at [ILM](/wiki/Industrial_Light_%26_Magic "Industrial Light & Magic"), with the animation and rendering done at [Lucasfilm Animation Singapore](/wiki/Lucasfilm_Animation_Singapore "Lucasfilm Animation Singapore"), and also [Polygon Pictures](/wiki/Polygon_Pictures "Polygon Pictures") between 2011 and 2013.[[62]](#cite_note-Polygon_Pictures-62) No rotoscoping was involved, however, ILM did use motion capture. The final assembly of each episode was done at [Skywalker Ranch](/wiki/Skywalker_Ranch "Skywalker Ranch").[[63]](#cite_note-3D_Star_Wars_Cartoon_News-63) Lucas's involvement resulted in rewrites of most of the scripts, as Lucas insisted on more character development and that the show should not be based in one location, but as many as possible so as to make the story as interesting as possible to the viewer.[[7]](#cite_note-Lucas_Involved-7) The animation style was inspired by 1960s-era puppets-in-space serials such as [Gerry Anderson's](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gerry_Anderson "wikipedia:Gerry Anderson") [*Thunderbirds*](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thunderbirds_(TV_series) "wikipedia:Thunderbirds (TV series)"),[[64]](#cite_note-TV-64) as well as the character designs from the original *Clone Wars* series.[[65]](#cite_note-Plunkett-65) Each episode of *The Clone Wars* was designed to be stand-alone, with an opening narration and moral to each story.[[66]](#cite_note-SWArchive-Introducing_Catherine_Winder-66) In terms of story and cinematography, the series was directed as if it were a live-action series,[[2]](#cite_note-CIVblog-2) and the episodes were produced in widescreen.[[67]](#cite_note-CWEW-67) Writer [Henry Gilroy](/wiki/Henry_Gilroy "Henry Gilroy") gained inspiration for the episode titles from the pulpy adventure sci-fi serials of the 1930s.[[68]](#cite_note-insider103-68) The series utilized unused ideas from Lucas' previous *Star Wars* projects.[[50]](#cite_note-nyt-50) [Paul Dini](/wiki/Paul_Dini "Paul Dini") pitched at least two rejected ideas for episodes: One involved [Jar Jar Binks](/wiki/Jar_Jar_Binks "Jar Jar Binks") trying to convince the [Galactic Senate](/wiki/Galactic_Senate "Galactic Senate") that there is life on an obscure planet, and the other involved [Anakin Skywalker](/wiki/Anakin_Skywalker "Anakin Skywalker") and [Padmé Amidala](/wiki/Padm%C3%A9_Amidala "Padmé Amidala") hiring an [Ewok](/wiki/Ewok "Ewok") assassin.[[69]](#cite_note-smodcast-69)

In 2008, In an interview they gave to TheForce.net, Filoni and Gilroy stated that, while Lucas gave them creative freedom for most of the series, there were several characters and locations that were off-limits. In respect to the characters, Lucas asked not to use [Han Solo](/wiki/Han_Solo "Han Solo"), [Chewbacca](/wiki/Chewbacca "Chewbacca"), [Boba Fett](/wiki/Boba_Fett "Boba Fett"), or [Jabba the Hutt](/wiki/Jabba_Desilijic_Tiure "Jabba Desilijic Tiure") when Gilroy was writing the show bible, but by the time of the next meeting, Lucas had changed his mind about the latter two characters. In respect to the locations, Lucas asked Gilroy and Filoni to not explore the planets seen in the films, with the exception of [Coruscant](/wiki/Coruscant "Coruscant"). But as with the character restrictions, he eventually changed his mind.[[70]](#cite_note-TFN_Gilroy_Filoni_interview-70)

In the same interview, Filoni stated, “We could come up with ideas and present them to [Lucas] immediately, so there was no concern as to whether or not it “was” Star Wars. This series at least to George is NOT EU, it is a part of Star Wars as he sees it. I think if anything there was a period where Henry and I had to learn exactly what it took to be a part of George Lucas’ Star Wars, and tell the Star Wars story his way. We had to learn how to look at the Galaxy from his point of view and let go of some of what we considered canon after we found out the ideas were only EU. Really we had to “unlearn what we had learned” and go back to the movies as the defining source material.”[[70]](#cite_note-TFN_Gilroy_Filoni_interview-70)  In the same year, in an interview featured in [Star Wars Insider 103](/wiki/Star_Wars_Insider_103 "Star Wars Insider 103"), Gilroy explained, Lucas wanted “a process where he could be involved creatively at every step.” He and Filoni generated the initial 15 or so story ideas, developing them into premises, then met with Lucas for his input and approval, which was repeated with the final script for the story. As time went on, however, Lucas started to write his own story outlines for the writers to craft them into scripts. Gilroy said, “George is the Alpha and the Omega, and is involved in the story from beginning to end. On *The Clone Wars*, that means from the initial story idea until the final sound mix” and that “just about every story now comes from ‘The Maker’ himself.”[[71]](#cite_note-Star_Wars_Insider_103-71)

On [March 11](/wiki/March_11 "March 11"), [2013](/wiki/2013 "2013"), a video appeared on [StarWars.com](/wiki/StarWars.com "StarWars.com"), in which the crew explained that they were "winding down" the production of the series, and that they had finished the active production of new episodes.[[72]](#cite_note-New_Direction-72) [Lucasfilm Story Group](/wiki/Lucasfilm_Story_Group "Lucasfilm Story Group")'s [Pablo Hidalgo](/wiki/Pablo_Hidalgo "Pablo Hidalgo") stated that there were 13 story arcs left unfinished.[[73]](#cite_note-Pablo_Hidalgo_Tweet-73) Writer [Brent Friedman](/wiki/Brent_Friedman "Brent Friedman") revealed on his Twitter account that scripts for the unproduced seasons 7 and 8 had been written prior to the series' cancelation.[[74]](#cite_note-Unaired-74) [James Arnold Taylor](/wiki/James_Arnold_Taylor "James Arnold Taylor"), [Obi-Wan Kenobi](/wiki/Obi-Wan_Kenobi "Obi-Wan Kenobi")'s voice actor, has stated that prior to the series' cancelation, the actors had recorded at least two remaining unproduced seasons.[[75]](#cite_note-JAT_Voice-75) Since the end of the series, both Leland Chee and the official blog have posted chronological lists of episodes.[[76]](#cite_note-Chee_Episode_List-76)[[77]](#cite_note-Order-77)

## Release and reception[]

 [![The exclusive Celebration IV poster for the series](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/d/dd/SWTCW-poster.jpg/revision/latest?cb=20070518031445) [![The exclusive Celebration IV poster for the series](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/d/dd/SWTCW-poster.jpg/revision/latest/scale-to-width-down/200?cb=20070518031445)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/d/dd/SWTCW-poster.jpg/revision/latest?cb=20070518031445) 

The exclusive Celebration IV poster for the series

 

The first [image](/wiki/File:SWtimeline.jpg "File:SWtimeline.jpg") released from the series—that of a 3D animated [Yoda](/wiki/Yoda "Yoda")—was shown at Toy Fair [2007](/wiki/2007 "2007").[[78]](#cite_note-78) On [May 27](/wiki/May_27 "May 27"), 2007, supervising director Dave Filoni and executive producer Catherine Winder gave a presentation at [Celebration IV](/wiki/Celebration_IV "Celebration IV") in which they debuted the first official trailer and poster, and discussed the production process of the previous two years.[[47]](#cite_note-Meet_the_Producer-47)[[79]](#cite_note-SWArchive-First_Look:_''The_Clone_Wars''_Celebration_IV_Poster-79) Filoni and Winder also held similar presentations at [Celebration Europe](/wiki/Celebration_Europe_(2007) "Celebration Europe (2007)") and WonderCon [2008](/wiki/2008 "2008").[[80]](#cite_note-SWArchive-''The_Clone_Wars''_at_Celebration_Europe-80)[[81]](#cite_note-SWArchive-''The_Clone_Wars''_News_Saturday_at_WonderCon-81) StarWars.com created a new division of the site dedicated to *The Clone Wars*, which was regularly updated with relevant content, including news articles, behind the scenes videos, and blog entries by [Pete Vilmur](/wiki/Pete_Vilmur "Pete Vilmur").[[82]](#cite_note-OfficialBlog-StarWars.com_Launches_''The_Clone_Wars''_Section-82)

### Television[]

Lucas shopped *The Clone Wars* to various networks, but had difficulty securing a buyer due to the show's unique tone.[[83]](#cite_note-BBC_SW-83) Fox Broadcasting passed on it, and Cartoon Network was initially unsure.[[50]](#cite_note-nyt-50) Several networks eventually got into a bidding war over the show.[[84]](#cite_note-sfg-84) [Cartoon Network](/wiki/Cartoon_Network "Cartoon Network") and [TNT](/wiki/Turner_Network_Television "Turner Network Television") eventually won the broadcast rights, with [Warner Bros.](/wiki/Warner_Bros. "Warner Bros.") distributing a theatrical debut. Warner had tracked the series' development, and decided on a theatrical launch after viewing some footage.[[85]](#cite_note-aswv-85) Stuart Snyder, former President of Cartoon Network, said he became interested in the new *Clone Wars* series immediately upon starting the job in May 2007. Snyder flew out to [San Francisco](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/San_Francisco,_California "wikipedia:San Francisco, California"), [California](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/California "wikipedia:California") to screen several episodes, and told Lucas the only place he wanted to see the show was on Cartoon Network.[[86]](#cite_note-AJC0902-86) It was announced on February 12, 2008 that the [feature film of the same name](/wiki/Star_Wars:_The_Clone_Wars_(film) "Star Wars: The Clone Wars (film)") was to be released in theaters on August 15, 2008, with the TV debut in the fall.[[3]](#cite_note-ann-3)[[87]](#cite_note-87)[[84]](#cite_note-sfg-84) This announcement was accompanied by an update of the Hyperspace online fan club kit,[[88]](#cite_note-88) and an offering of [Captain Rex](/wiki/Rex "Rex") and [Ahsoka Tano](/wiki/Ahsoka_Tano "Ahsoka Tano") T-shirts to Hyperspace members.[[89]](#cite_note-Shirt-89)[[90]](#cite_note-SWArchive-Hyperspace_Exclusive_Ahsoka_T-shirt-90)

The series premiered on October 3, 2008 at 9 p.m. on the Cartoon Network. It aired on Friday nights[[91]](#cite_note-CW_Air-91) as part of an [action-adventure](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Action-adventure "wikipedia:Action-adventure") block alongside [*The Secret Saturdays*](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Secret_Saturdays "wikipedia:The Secret Saturdays") and [*Ben 10: Alien Force*](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ben_10:_Alien_Force "wikipedia:Ben 10: Alien Force"), in an attempt to rejuvenate the network and compete with channels, such as [Nickelodeon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nickelodeon_(TV_channel) "wikipedia:Nickelodeon (TV channel)") and the [Disney Channel](/wiki/Disney_Channel "Disney Channel"). Snyder expressed confidence that the shows would help boost ratings: "You catch me at a time where I have a smile on my face because of our internal results," Snyder said. "I can say there's a little bit of bragging on the third quarter for us."[[86]](#cite_note-AJC0902-86) In Canada, the first season aired on [CTV](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/CTV_Television_Network "wikipedia:CTV Television Network")[[92]](#cite_note-92) and [SPACE](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_(TV_channel) "wikipedia:Space (TV channel)"), while the second through fifth aired on [Teletoon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Teletoon_(Canadian_TV_channel) "wikipedia:Teletoon (Canadian TV channel)"), which aired repeats of the first season as part of its Weekday Action Force block. In Australia, the first season aired on Channel Ten. On April 13, 2011, ABC3 aired repeats of first season and has since aired seasons two, three, and four. During May 4-5, ABC3 did a marathon of all Season 5 episodes, which was the first time Season 5 had aired on ABC3. The series was first aired in the UK on [Sky Movies](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sky_Movies "wikipedia:Sky Movies") Premiere and Premiere HD every Saturday at 5.30PM with the first episode aired on October 25, 2008. As with all programs on Sky Movies, it ran for the first 22-minutes of its 30-minute slot with advertisements shown at the end so as not to interrupt the episodes.[[93]](#cite_note-Sky-93)[[94]](#cite_note-Sky_Debut-94)

Lucas expected *The Clone Wars* to run for four or five years, but planned to produce at least 100 episodes regardless of ratings.[[95]](#cite_note-comingsoon-95)[[67]](#cite_note-CWEW-67)[[96]](#cite_note-Lucas_TV-96)[[97]](#cite_note-Lucas_UK_TV-97)[[98]](#cite_note-TVGuide-98) The first four seasons consisted of 22 episodes, the fifth of 20 episodes, and the sixth of 13 episodes. The [21st](/wiki/Brothers_(episode) "Brothers (episode)") and [22nd](/wiki/Revenge_(episode) "Revenge (episode)") episodes of [Season Four](/wiki/The_Clone_Wars:_Season_Four "The Clone Wars: Season Four") featured a red opening logo, as opposed to the series' standard yellow.[[99]](#cite_note-''Brothers''_Trivia_Gallery-99) In the [10th](/wiki/Secret_Weapons "Secret Weapons"), [11th](/wiki/A_Sunny_Day_in_the_Void "A Sunny Day in the Void"), [12th](/wiki/Missing_in_Action "Missing in Action"), and [13th](/wiki/Point_of_No_Return_(The_Clone_Wars) "Point of No Return (The Clone Wars)") episodes of [Season Five](/wiki/The_Clone_Wars:_Season_Five "The Clone Wars: Season Five"), the opening logo was changed to have a blue color in honor of [R2-D2](/wiki/R2-D2 "R2-D2"). TNT signed a multi-seasonal agreement to broadcast repeats of the series,[[100]](#cite_note-tvgqa-100)[[101]](#cite_note-SWArchive-''The_Clone_Wars''_Premieres_on_TNT_in_February-101) though only aired a limited run before dropping the series.[[102]](#cite_note-forcenet-102) Episodes began airing in syndication in fall 2012, in conjunction with the series' fifth season.[[103]](#cite_note-Syndication-103)

### Post-cancellation[]

An abridged sixth season, dubbed [The Lost Missions](/wiki/The_Clone_Wars:_The_Lost_Missions "The Clone Wars: The Lost Missions"), was released in the United States through [Netflix](/wiki/Netflix "Netflix") and in Germany on [Super RTL](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Super_RTL "wikipedia:Super RTL").[[4]](#cite_note-TCW_on_Netflix-4)[[104]](#cite_note-German_TV_Schedule-104) (The Netflix episodes were part of a package deal that included the feature film and the first five seasons.[[4]](#cite_note-TCW_on_Netflix-4)) However, Cartoon Network sometimes used the sixth season episodes. Additional episodes were released in the form of [*The Clone Wars* Legacy](/wiki/The_Clone_Wars_Legacy "The Clone Wars Legacy"), a project that encompasses the comic book series [*Star Wars: Darth Maul—Son of Dathomir*](/wiki/Star_Wars:_Darth_Maul_%E2%80%94_Son_of_Dathomir "Star Wars: Darth Maul — Son of Dathomir"), the novel *[Dark Disciple](/wiki/Dark_Disciple "Dark Disciple")*, and 8 story reels that were posted to StarWars.com but were later taken off the site.[[105]](#cite_note-TCW_Legacy-105)

The series proved extremely popular with a loyal core of fans, who repeatedly petitioned for the revival of the series, often using the social media hashtag #SaveTheCloneWars. At the [2018](/wiki/2018 "2018") [San Diego Comic-Con](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/San_Diego_Comic-Con "wikipedia:San Diego Comic-Con"), Dave Filoni led a panel celebrating the tenth anniversary of the series. The end of the panel saw the announcement that a [final set of episodes](/wiki/The_Clone_Wars:_Season_Seven "The Clone Wars: Season Seven") would be released on the [Disney+](/wiki/Disney%2B "Disney+") in [2020](/wiki/2020 "2020"). Filoni credited the immense fan support as being key in Disney's decision to revive the series.[[5]](#cite_note-TCW_Revival-5) To commemorate the completion of the final season, the cast held a [D23](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/D23_(Disney) "wikipedia:D23 (Disney)") livestream on [May 8](/wiki/May_8 "May 8"), [2020](/wiki/2020 "2020").[[106]](#cite_note-D23-106)

## Continuity[]

The series's creators explained that continuity with the [Expanded Universe](/wiki/Star_Wars_Legends "Star Wars Legends") was being taken very seriously, with Dave Filoni being well-versed in the material (although Lucas had the right to make slight adjustments for the sake of the story, and was consulted directly when dealing with the major characters).[[2]](#cite_note-CIVblog-2) Lucasfilm told *TV Guide* that *The Clone Wars* would not supersede the original *Clone Wars* series in continuity, but would expand upon what the earlier series established.[[100]](#cite_note-tvgqa-100) Dark Horse Comics editor [Randy Stradley](/wiki/Randy_Stradley "Randy Stradley") also claimed to have met with Lucasfilm Animation to discuss integrating the show with the [*Clone Wars* comics](/wiki/Star_Wars:_Clone_Wars_(trade_paperbacks) "Star Wars: Clone Wars (trade paperbacks)").[[107]](#cite_note-DH_Staff-107) However, the feature film and TV series introduced a number of continuity inconsistencies, many of which directly contradicted previously published sources and required [retcons](/wiki/Retroactive_continuity "Retroactive continuity") and major shifts in the previously established Clone Wars timeline which were never established by [Leland Chee](/wiki/Leland_Chee "Leland Chee").[[108]](#cite_note-DH_Chee-108) There were several prominent examples of direct contradiction between *The Clone Wars* and previous *Clone Wars* media:

* On [August 8](/wiki/August_8 "August 8"), 2009, *[Republic Commando](/wiki/Republic_Commando "Republic Commando")* author [Karen Traviss](/wiki/Karen_Traviss "Karen Traviss") stated that she was leaving the *Star Wars* franchise due to alleged continuity issues raised with the publication of *[The Art of Star Wars: The Clone Wars](/wiki/The_Art_of_Star_Wars:_The_Clone_Wars "The Art of Star Wars: The Clone Wars")*,[[109]](#cite_note-109) which included details regarding the [Mandalorians](/wiki/Mandalorian/Legends "Mandalorian/Legends") that clashed with the continuity set-up by her novels; this was most likely in reference to the trilogy of episodes involving [Mandalore](/wiki/Mandalore "Mandalore") in the show’s second season ("[The Mandalore Plot](/wiki/The_Mandalore_Plot "The Mandalore Plot")," "[Voyage of Temptation](/wiki/Voyage_of_Temptation "Voyage of Temptation")" and "[Duchess of Mandalore](/wiki/Duchess_of_Mandalore "Duchess of Mandalore")") in which the main Mandalorian faction is portrayed as a pacifist society living on Mandalore, which itself is portrayed as a radioactive desert, contradicting all previous descriptions.[[110]](#cite_note-TMP-110) Prior to the April 25, 2014, reorganization of canon, Leland Chee[[111]](#cite_note-111) and [Sue Rostoni](/wiki/Sue_Rostoni "Sue Rostoni") maintained that the complications would eventually be worked-out.[[112]](#cite_note-112) The two portrayals of the planet were reconciled with retcons issued by *[The Essential Atlas](/wiki/The_Essential_Atlas "The Essential Atlas")* and the subsequent *[Star Wars: The Clone Wars: New Battlefronts: The Visual Guide](/wiki/Star_Wars:_The_Clone_Wars:_New_Battlefronts:_The_Visual_Guide "Star Wars: The Clone Wars: New Battlefronts: The Visual Guide")*, which states that (much like Earth) the vast, white-sand deserts seen in the aforementioned episodes was but one region of the larger, varied landscape of Mandalore's surface.
* The use of [Eta-2 *Actis*-class interceptors](/wiki/Eta-2_Actis-class_light_interceptor "Eta-2 Actis-class light interceptor") at the same point in the timeline Anakin is knighted,[[113]](#cite_note-Clone_Wars-113) whereas in *The Clone Wars* [Delta-7B *Aethersprite*-class light interceptors](/wiki/Delta-7B_Aethersprite-class_light_interceptor "Delta-7B Aethersprite-class light interceptor") are used, which were ostensibly used before the later Eta-2s. In addition, some elements from works like the [novelization of *Revenge of the Sith*](/wiki/Star_Wars:_Revenge_of_the_Sith_(novelization) "Star Wars: Revenge of the Sith (novelization)") are being retconned. For example, in the novelization, Anakin remarks that he has only read about [Grievous](/wiki/Grievous "Grievous")' [IG-100 MagnaGuards](/wiki/IG-100_MagnaGuard "IG-100 MagnaGuard") in an intel report, despite having fought them in the show.[[114]](#cite_note-DotD-114) Another very noticeable continuity error is the fact that Anakin has his scar, which he received shortly after the [Battle of Rendili](/wiki/Battle_of_Rendili "Battle of Rendili") from [Asajj Ventress](/wiki/Asajj_Ventress "Asajj Ventress"). He then injured Ventress so severely that she was forced to recuperate until the [Battle of Boz Pity](/wiki/Battle_of_Boz_Pity_(Clone_Wars) "Battle of Boz Pity (Clone Wars)"), after which she deserted the CIS and the war for good. However, he was originally shown to receive his scar in [20 BBY](/wiki/20_BBY/Legends "20 BBY/Legends"), while the series begins in [22 BBY](/wiki/22_BBY/Legends "22 BBY/Legends").
* In 2003, the reference book *[Inside the Worlds of Star Wars: Attack of the Clones](/wiki/Inside_the_Worlds_of_Star_Wars:_Attack_of_the_Clones "Inside the Worlds of Star Wars: Attack of the Clones")* established that Jedi Master [Eeth Koth](/wiki/Eeth_Koth "Eeth Koth") died during the [First Battle of Geonosis](/wiki/First_Battle_of_Geonosis "First Battle of Geonosis") when enemy fire brought down his gunship. However, the character was "resurrected" by the project; he was first mentioned as fighting in the Clone Wars in the 2008 novel *[The Clone Wars: Wild Space](/wiki/The_Clone_Wars:_Wild_Space "The Clone Wars: Wild Space")* and was later featured prominently in the second-season episode "[Grievous Intrigue](/wiki/Grievous_Intrigue "Grievous Intrigue")."
* The third season saw an evolution in the appearance of the main and supporting characters along wit. Ahsoka Tano's new attire represented a more mature look. Anakin Skywalker and Obi-Wan Kenobi's attire was adjusted to be closer to how they appeared in [*Revenge of the Sith*](/wiki/Star_Wars:_Episode_III_Revenge_of_the_Sith "Star Wars: Episode III Revenge of the Sith").[[115]](#cite_note-New_Look-115)
* In the third season episode "[Citadel Rescue](/wiki/Citadel_Rescue "Citadel Rescue")," Jedi Master [Even Piell](/wiki/Even_Piell "Even Piell") died during a [mission](/wiki/Battle_of_Lola_Sayu "Battle of Lola Sayu") around the second year of the war. In the 2008 novel *[Coruscant Nights I: Jedi Twilight](/wiki/Coruscant_Nights_I:_Jedi_Twilight "Coruscant Nights I: Jedi Twilight")*, written by [Michael Reaves](/wiki/Michael_Reaves "Michael Reaves"), [Even Piell](/wiki/Even_Piell/Legends "Even Piell/Legends") lived through the Clone Wars and died during the [Great Jedi Purge](/wiki/Great_Jedi_Purge/Legends "Great Jedi Purge/Legends") in 19 BBY on Coruscant.
* StarWars.com confirmed that Darth Maul survived the [Battle of Naboo](/wiki/Battle_of_Naboo "Battle of Naboo") and would appear in [Season Four](/wiki/The_Clone_Wars:_Season_Four "The Clone Wars: Season Four") of the series.[[116]](#cite_note-He's_Back!-116) Maul returned in the [21st episode](/wiki/Brothers_(episode) "Brothers (episode)"), living on [Lotho Minor](/wiki/Lotho_Minor "Lotho Minor").
* The fifth-season opener "[Revival](/wiki/Revival_(episode) "Revival (episode)")" featured the death of Jedi Master [Adi Gallia](/wiki/Adi_Gallia "Adi Gallia") by Savage Opress [on](/wiki/Skirmish_on_Florrum "Skirmish on Florrum") [Florrum](/wiki/Florrum "Florrum"), despite having previously been slain by Grievous during the [Battle of Boz Pity](/wiki/Battle_of_Boz_Pity_(Clone_Wars) "Battle of Boz Pity (Clone Wars)"), one of the final battles of the Clone Wars in the 2005 comic [*Obsession* 5](/wiki/Obsession_5 "Obsession 5").
* The fifth season finale "[The Wrong Jedi](/wiki/The_Wrong_Jedi "The Wrong Jedi")" presented that [Barriss Offee](/wiki/Barriss_Offee "Barriss Offee") fell to the [dark side of the Force](/wiki/Dark_side_of_the_Force "Dark side of the Force") and [destroys](/wiki/Bombing_of_the_Jedi_Temple_hangar "Bombing of the Jedi Temple hangar") the [Jedi Temple](/wiki/Jedi_Temple/Legends "Jedi Temple/Legends") hangar, framing Ahsoka Tano, and [initiating](/wiki/Trial_of_Ahsoka_Tano "Trial of Ahsoka Tano") an investigation against Tano, but Anakin ultimately discovers her plot and Offee gets arrested and taken away to prison. However, the daily webstrips series *[Reversal of Fortune](/wiki/Reversal_of_Fortune "Reversal of Fortune")* and the [Databank](/wiki/Databank_(original) "Databank (original)") entry of [Felucia](/wiki/Felucia "Felucia") originally stated that [Barriss Offee](/wiki/Barriss_Offee/Legends "Barriss Offee/Legends") was killed at the end of the Clone Wars during [Order 66](/wiki/Order_66/Legends "Order 66/Legends") on [Felucia](/wiki/Felucia/Legends "Felucia/Legends"), reflecting the original version of Order 66 in [*Star Wars*: Episode III *Revenge of the Sith*](/wiki/Star_Wars:_Episode_III_Revenge_of_the_Sith "Star Wars: Episode III Revenge of the Sith"), in which Offee was to die along [Luminara Unduli](/wiki/Luminara_Unduli "Luminara Unduli") and [Shaak Ti](/wiki/Shaak_Ti "Shaak Ti"), whose death scenes were too omitted.[[117]](#cite_note-Original_Fate-117) As Offee was depicted as still serving the [Jedi Order](/wiki/Jedi_Order/Legends "Jedi Order/Legends"), it has been assumed in the Expanded Universe continuity that Offee remained at the Order through unknown reasons. Furthermore, Offee was intended to originally kill herself at the end of the episode, which would have contradicted her post-*The Clone Wars* EU appearances definitively, but Dave Filoni cut the scene because he "had plans" for the character, which ultimately never came to fruition by the show's cancelation.[[118]](#cite_note-untold-118)
* If the show had not been canceled, there was going to be an episode arc in the seventh season focusing on [Maul](/wiki/Maul "Maul"), which would have delved into his origins. While the episodes went unmade, their scripts were adapted into [Dark Horse Comics](/wiki/Dark_Horse_Comics "Dark Horse Comics")' comic book series [*Star Wars: Darth Maul—Son of Dathomir*](/wiki/Star_Wars:_Darth_Maul_%E2%80%94_Son_of_Dathomir "Star Wars: Darth Maul — Son of Dathomir"), which revealed [Mother](/wiki/Mother_(title) "Mother (title)") [Talzin](/wiki/Talzin "Talzin") to be Maul's mother, as well [Savage Opress](/wiki/Savage_Opress "Savage Opress")'. However, the novel *[Darth Plagueis](/wiki/Darth_Plagueis "Darth Plagueis")* had previously established that a [Human](/wiki/Human/Legends "Human/Legends") [Nightsister](/wiki/Nightsisters/Legends "Nightsisters/Legends") named [Kycina](/wiki/Kycina "Kycina") was [Maul's](/wiki/Darth_Maul/Legends "Darth Maul/Legends") mother, and the short story *[Restraint](/wiki/Restraint "Restraint")* identified her as [Opress](/wiki/Savage_Opress/Legends "Savage Opress/Legends")' mother as well.
* One of the unproduced episodes due the show's cancelation would have featured the [Yuuzhan Vong](/wiki/Yuuzhan_Vong "Yuuzhan Vong"), the extra-galactic species which first appeared in [Del Rey](/wiki/Del_Rey "Del Rey")'s [1999](/wiki/1999 "1999")-[2003](/wiki/2003 "2003") book series *[Star Wars: The New Jedi Order](/wiki/Star_Wars:_The_New_Jedi_Order "Star Wars: The New Jedi Order")*. According to [Pablo Hidalgo](/wiki/Pablo_Hidalgo "Pablo Hidalgo"), the episode wouldn't have specified the Vong's origins but only imply that they came from [another galaxy](/wiki/Yuuzhan_Vong_galaxy "Yuuzhan Vong galaxy"), just as *[The New Jedi Order: Vector Prime](/wiki/The_New_Jedi_Order:_Vector_Prime "The New Jedi Order: Vector Prime")* originally established.[[119]](#cite_note-Pablo_Hidalgo_Vong_Tweet_02-119) However, Hidalgo has stated that per George Lucas' vision of the Force, the Yuuzhan Vong weren't immune to the Force in the story.[[120]](#cite_note-Vong_Force_Immunity-120) This would have contradicted the EU, as the Yuuzhan Vong were established as immune to the Force (except to the [Force lightning](/wiki/Force_lightning/Legends "Force lightning/Legends") and [Force net](/wiki/Force_net "Force net") attacks) in *[The New Jedi Order: Edge of Victory I: Conquest](/wiki/The_New_Jedi_Order:_Edge_of_Victory_I:_Conquest "The New Jedi Order: Edge of Victory I: Conquest")*.
* Likewise, in a similar way to Barriss Offee and the Yuuzhan Vong, [Jaime King](/wiki/Jaime_King "Jaime King")'s husband, Kyle Newman has stated that there were several unfinished episodes planned for the sixth season of the show featuring [Aurra Sing](/wiki/Aurra_Sing "Aurra Sing"), including one in which Sing was to be killed.[[121]](#cite_note-Aurra's_Planned_Death-121) Had this been canonized, it would have contradicted several of [Aurra Sing's](/wiki/Aurra_Sing/Legends "Aurra Sing/Legends") appearances in EU stories set during the [Galactic Civil War](/wiki/Galactic_Civil_War/Legends "Galactic Civil War/Legends") and the [New Republic](/wiki/New_Republic_era "New Republic era") and [New Jedi Order eras](/wiki/New_Jedi_Order_era "New Jedi Order era"), precisely *[Coruscant Nights II: Street of Shadows](/wiki/Coruscant_Nights_II:_Street_of_Shadows "Coruscant Nights II: Street of Shadows")*, *[Star Wars: Demolition](/wiki/Star_Wars:_Demolition "Star Wars: Demolition")*, and *[Legacy of the Force: Tempest](/wiki/Legacy_of_the_Force:_Tempest "Legacy of the Force: Tempest")*. Eventually, in the new Canon continuity Sing's fate was addressed in the [*Star Wars* Anthology](/wiki/Star_Wars_Anthology_Series "Star Wars Anthology Series") film, *[Solo: A Star Wars Story](/wiki/Solo:_A_Star_Wars_Story "Solo: A Star Wars Story")*, in which it was established that [Tobias Beckett](/wiki/Tobias_Beckett "Tobias Beckett") pushed Sing to her death.

Initially supervising director Dave Filoni defended any differences in continuity: "But there's never an implicit connection between the micro-series that Cartoon Network did previously and the series that we're doing now. I personally as a fan never think of it as discrediting any of the other material, it's just that other material is from a different point of view, a different look at the war and take on the war. It's an ever-Expanding Universe in a lot of ways."[[122]](#cite_note-Diloni_CBR-122) At his Celebration IV presentations, Filoni showed a series of slides showing several character sculpture designs for the series—stating that they would share some of the stylization of the original *Clone Wars* series, but would also have some of the realistic look of the films. He explained, however, that elements of the series would differ slightly from what has been previously established in continuity.[[123]](#cite_note-QA-123) Changes were made from the original *Clone Wars* series: Obi-Wan doesn't wear as much of his clone general armor, Grievous has a cough prior to the [Battle of Coruscant](/wiki/Battle_of_Coruscant "Battle of Coruscant"),[[123]](#cite_note-QA-123) and the Jedi fighting styles are more like the films, and not like some of the exaggerated Jedi abilities portrayed in the original series.[[2]](#cite_note-CIVblog-2) Eventually Filoni would go on record to state that the Expanded Universe and *The Clone Wars* television series "don't live in the same universe".[[124]](#cite_note-Insider_134-124)

*The Clone Wars* was classified as [T-canon](/wiki/Canon "Canon") in the [Holocron continuity database](/wiki/Holocron_continuity_database "Holocron continuity database").[[125]](#cite_note-T-canon-125)[[126]](#cite_note-CHEE_Forum-126) However, on [April 25](/wiki/April_25 "April 25"), 2014, it was announced that the Expanded Universe was to be re-branded as *Star Wars* Legends and that the only past material that would be considered canon would be the [original trilogy](/wiki/Original_trilogy "Original trilogy") and [prequel trilogy](/wiki/Prequel_trilogy "Prequel trilogy") films and *The Clone Wars,* while also enshrining Episodes 1-6 and The Clone Wars as the immovable truth for both timelines, thus negating any concerns regarding conflicts between the series and past *Star Wars* Legends material for content that was produced in the Canon timeline. Novelizations based on the series, however, are not considered canon, nor are video game releases or comics, with the exception of Legacy material and any other upcoming projects based on material that was developed for the television series that ultimately did not make it to broadcast.[[127]](#cite_note-End_of_EU-127)[[128]](#cite_note-SDCC_Live_Blog-128) Reference works based on the series, such as *[Star Wars: The Clone Wars Character Encyclopedia](/wiki/Star_Wars:_The_Clone_Wars_Character_Encyclopedia "Star Wars: The Clone Wars Character Encyclopedia")*, are considered part of the "Legends" continuity and are not considered canon sources, albeit a canonical [reference titles](/wiki/Star_Wars:_The_Clone_Wars:_Character_Encyclopedia_-_Join_the_Battle! "Star Wars: The Clone Wars: Character Encyclopedia - Join the Battle!") now exist for the series' characters. As a consequence of the 2014 reboot, the initial multimedia project for the series was rendered non-canonical to the current continuity.

## Adaptations and tie-in media[]

[Sue Rostoni](/wiki/Sue_Rostoni "Sue Rostoni") first stated in June 2007 that a publishing program based on the series was possible, but had not yet been discussed.[[129]](#cite_note-129) [Rob Coleman](/wiki/Rob_Coleman "Rob Coleman") reported that licensees had a very positive reaction upon first seeing footage from the series.[[130]](#cite_note-Hyperspace-Frank_Oz_and_Rob_Coleman_Q&A:_DVD_Press_Event-130)[[63]](#cite_note-3D_Star_Wars_Cartoon_News-63) A [Dark Horse Comics](/wiki/Dark_Horse_Comics "Dark Horse Comics") volume was made for [Free Comic Book Day](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Free_Comic_Book_Day "wikipedia:Free Comic Book Day").[[131]](#cite_note-Free_Comic-131) To accompany the [Season One](/wiki/The_Clone_Wars:_Season_One "The Clone Wars: Season One") episodes, StarWars.com hosted a [weekly web comic](/wiki/Star_Wars:_The_Clone_Wars_(webcomics) "Star Wars: The Clone Wars (webcomics)"), as well as a [HoloNet News](/wiki/HoloNet_News_(original_website) "HoloNet News (original website)") podcast. The episodes were available on iTunes the day after they aired, and on StarWars.com and CartoonNetwork.com a week after they aired.[[132]](#cite_note-CW_Support-132) From 2008 to 2010, Lucasfilm sponsored *The Clone Wars*-themed exhibits in certain major US cities.[[133]](#cite_note-CW_Exhibit-133)[[134]](#cite_note-CW_Exhibition-134)[[135]](#cite_note-CW_SC-135)[[136]](#cite_note-SWArchive-''The_Clone_Wars''_Weekend_at_Zeum-136)

Characters from *The Clone Wars* were added to a DLC expansion of *[Star Wars Battlefront II](/wiki/Star_Wars_Battlefront_II "Star Wars Battlefront II")*.[[137]](#cite_note-CW_BF2-137)[[138]](#cite_note-EA_Play-138)[[139]](#cite_note-BF2_Fighter-139) Hasbro will also produce new *The Clone Wars* toys.[[140]](#cite_note-SDCC_2018-140)

### Home video[]

Each season prior to the seventh received complete [DVD and Blu ray releases](/wiki/Star_Wars_home_video_releases "Star Wars home video releases"):

* [*Star Wars: The Clone Wars*: The Complete Season One](/wiki/Star_Wars:_The_Clone_Wars_The_Complete_Season_One "Star Wars: The Clone Wars The Complete Season One")
* [*Star Wars: The Clone Wars*: The Complete Season Two](/wiki/Star_Wars:_The_Clone_Wars_The_Complete_Season_Two "Star Wars: The Clone Wars The Complete Season Two")
* [*Star Wars: The Clone Wars*: The Complete Season Three](/wiki/Star_Wars:_The_Clone_Wars_The_Complete_Season_Three "Star Wars: The Clone Wars The Complete Season Three")
* [*Star Wars: The Clone Wars*: The Complete Season Four](/wiki/Star_Wars:_The_Clone_Wars_The_Complete_Season_Four "Star Wars: The Clone Wars The Complete Season Four")
* [*Star Wars: The Clone Wars*: The Complete Season Five](/wiki/Star_Wars:_The_Clone_Wars_The_Complete_Season_Five "Star Wars: The Clone Wars The Complete Season Five")
* [*Star Wars: The Clone Wars*: The Lost Missions](/wiki/Star_Wars:_The_Clone_Wars_%E2%80%93_The_Lost_Missions "Star Wars: The Clone Wars – The Lost Missions")

A [Collector's Edition boxed set](/wiki/Star_Wars:_The_Clone_Wars_Seasons_1-5_Collector%27s_Edition "Star Wars: The Clone Wars Seasons 1-5 Collector's Edition") of the first five seasons was released in 2013.[[141]](#cite_note-CW_S5-141)

Three themed collections of episodes were released: ["Bounty Hunters"](/wiki/Star_Wars:_Greatest_Bounty_Hunters "Star Wars: Greatest Bounty Hunters"), ["Clone Commandos"](/wiki/Star_Wars:_The_Clone_Wars:_Clone_Commandos "Star Wars: The Clone Wars: Clone Commandos"), and [*Darth Maul Returns*](/wiki/Star_Wars:_The_Clone_Wars:_Darth_Maul_Returns "Star Wars: The Clone Wars: Darth Maul Returns") (a feature-length edit of a [Season Four](/wiki/The_Clone_Wars:_Season_Four "The Clone Wars: Season Four") arc). A feature-length edit of a [Season Three](/wiki/The_Clone_Wars:_Season_Three "The Clone Wars: Season Three") arc entitled *[The Nightsisters Trilogy: Feature-Length Cut](/wiki/The_Nightsisters_Trilogy:_Feature-Length_Cut "The Nightsisters Trilogy: Feature-Length Cut")* was released exclusively on iTunes.

A series of [Walmart](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Walmart "wikipedia:Walmart")-exclusive DVDs were bundled with certain action figure sets from 2010 to 2012. Each DVD featured one episode from the series, as well as a trailer for that season's respective DVD release.[[142]](#cite_note-Hasbro_Gallery-142)[[143]](#cite_note-Hasbro_Next-143)[[144]](#cite_note-Legacy_of_Terror_Pack-144)[[145]](#cite_note-Brain_Invaders_Pack-145) [Target](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Target_Corporation "wikipedia:Target Corporation") also included an exclusive DVD included in the 2010 action figure sets "Hostage Crisis" and "The Hidden Enemy".[[146]](#cite_note-Hidden_Enemy_Pack-146)

## Reception ‡[]

The series debuted on October 3, 2008 with the episode "[Ambush](/wiki/Ambush "Ambush")," which brought in 3.96 million viewers,[[147]](#cite_note-CW_Variety-147) and was the channel's most watched series premiere.[[148]](#cite_note-CW_HR-148) [Season Two](/wiki/The_Clone_Wars:_Season_Two "The Clone Wars: Season Two") premiered on October 2, 2009 with the episodes "[Holocron Heist](/wiki/Holocron_Heist "Holocron Heist")" and "[Cargo of Doom](/wiki/Cargo_of_Doom "Cargo of Doom")," which averaged 2.58 million viewers.[[149]](#cite_note-TVBTR-149)

The first season episode "[Lair of Grievous](/wiki/Lair_of_Grievous "Lair of Grievous")" won a [Golden Reel Award](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Golden_Reel_Award_(Motion_Picture_Sound_Editors) "wikipedia:Golden Reel Award (Motion Picture Sound Editors)") for best sound editing in television animation.[[150]](#cite_note-Hollywood_Reporter_Golden_Reel-150) The series was nominated for the 2009 [Saturn](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saturn_awards "wikipedia:Saturn awards") Award for "Best Cable/Syndicated TV Series."[[151]](#cite_note-Saturn-151) At the [40th Daytime Emmy Awards](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/40th_Daytime_Emmy_Awards "wikipedia:40th Daytime Emmy Awards") on [June 16](/wiki/June_16 "June 16"), 2013, *The Clone Wars* won two [Daytime Emmy Awards](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Daytime_Emmy_Award "wikipedia:Daytime Emmy Award"). [David Tennant](/wiki/David_Tennant "David Tennant")'s performance of Professor [Huyang](/wiki/Huyang "Huyang") in the fifth season episodes "[A Test of Strength](/wiki/A_Test_of_Strength "A Test of Strength")" and "[A Necessary Bond](/wiki/A_Necessary_Bond "A Necessary Bond")" won him the Outstanding Performer in an Animated Program, while the series itself garnered the Outstanding Special Class Animated Program award.[[152]](#cite_note-TCW_Wins_2_Emmys-152) In 2014, the series was also nominated for four daytime Emmys,[[153]](#cite_note-Emmys-153)[[154]](#cite_note-EmmyOnline-154) winning two.[[155]](#cite_note-Two_Emmys-155) In 2021, the series' revived seventh season was nominated for three Emmys.[[156]](#cite_note-Final_Emmys-156)
